# rw_backend/../daemon.py (LAP TIMING DIAGNOSTIC)

import threading
import time
from queue import Queue
from datetime import datetime

from rw_backend.simulators.lmu.collector import LMUCollector
from rw_backend.handlers.session_handler import SessionHandler
from rw_backend.handlers.stint_handler import StintHandler
from rw_backend.database.manager import initialize_database, connect_db, close_db


def Cbytestring2Python(bytestring):
    try: return bytes(bytestring).partition(b'\0')[0].decode('utf-8').strip()
    except: return ""

class LapTimingDiagnostic(threading.Thread):
    # --- Use the agreed upon 30Hz frequency ---
    LOGGING_FREQUENCY = 30  # Hz
    BURST_LOG_DURATION = 2.0 # seconds

    def __init__(self, raw_data_queue: Queue, session_handler, stint_handler):
        super().__init__(daemon=True)
        self.raw_data_queue = raw_data_queue
        self._running = threading.Event()

        # State Tracking
        self.track_length = 0.0
        self.last_player_data = {}
        self.last_extended_data = {}
        self.player_state = "UNKNOWN"
        self.burst_log_end_time = 0.0

        # Handlers for context
        self.session_handler = session_handler
        self.stint_handler = stint_handler

    def run(self):
        print(f"[{datetime.now().strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S.%f')[:-3]}] [INFO] Lap Timing Diagnostic thread started.", flush=True)
        self._running.set()
        
        while self._running.is_set():
            raw_data = self.raw_data_queue.get()
            if raw_data is None: break

            extended = raw_data.get('extended')
            if not extended or not extended.mSessionStarted:
                time.sleep(0.5)
                continue
            
            scoring = raw_data.get('scoring')
            player_scoring = next((v for v in scoring.mVehicles if v.mIsPlayer), None) if scoring else None
            
            if not player_scoring:
                time.sleep(0.5)
                continue

            if self.track_length == 0.0:
                 self.track_length = scoring.mScoringInfo.mLapDist

            # --- Logging Trigger Logic ---
            should_log_now = False
            
            # Trigger 1: Near the Start/Finish line
            is_near_sf = (self.track_length > 0) and \
                         ((self.track_length - 200) < player_scoring.mLapDist or player_scoring.mLapDist < 200)
            
            # Trigger 2: A sector has just changed
            current_sector = player_scoring.mSector
            last_sector = self.last_player_data.get('mSector', -1)
            if current_sector != last_sector and last_sector != -1:
                print(f"[{datetime.now().strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S.%f')[:-3]}] [INFO] Sector change detected ({last_sector} -> {current_sector}). Starting log burst.", flush=True)
                self.burst_log_end_time = time.monotonic() + self.BURST_LOG_DURATION
            
            # Trigger 3: We are currently inside a log burst
            is_in_burst = time.monotonic() < self.burst_log_end_time

            should_log_now = is_near_sf or is_in_burst

            if should_log_now:
                self._log_diagnostic_frame(raw_data, player_scoring)
            
            self.last_player_data = {field[0]: getattr(player_scoring, field[0]) for field in player_scoring._fields_}

            if should_log_now:
                time.sleep(1 / self.LOGGING_FREQUENCY)
            else:
                time.sleep(1 / 10) # Poll reasonably fast to not miss sector changes

    def _log_diagnostic_frame(self, raw_data, player_scoring):
        ts = datetime.now().strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S.%f')[:-3]
        telemetry = raw_data['telemetry']
        
        app_stint_num = self.stint_handler.current_stint_model.stint_number if self.stint_handler.current_stint_model else 'None'
        
        log_line = (
            f"[{ts}] [DIAG-FRAME] "
            # Identity & Position
            f"Lap={player_scoring.mTotalLaps} "
            f"Sector={player_scoring.mSector} "
            f"LapDist={player_scoring.mLapDist:.2f} "
            # Master Clock
            f"ElapsedTime={telemetry.mElapsedTime:.3f} "
            # Lap Timers
            f"LapStartET={player_scoring.mLapStartET:.3f} "
            f"TimeIntoLap={player_scoring.mTimeIntoLap:.3f} "
            # Current Sector Timers
            f"CurSec1={player_scoring.mCurSector1:.3f} "
            f"CurSec2={player_scoring.mCurSector2:.3f} "
            # Last Lap Timers
            f"LastLapTime={player_scoring.mLastLapTime:.3f} "
            f"LastSec1={player_scoring.mLastSector1:.3f} "
            f"LastSec2={player_scoring.mLastSector2:.3f} "
            # App Context
            f"|| AppPlayerState={self.player_state} AppStintNum={app_stint_num}"
        )
        print(log_line, flush=True)

    def stop(self):
        self._running.clear()
        self.raw_data_queue.put(None)

# Simplified run_daemon for this specific diagnostic
def run_daemon():
    print(f"[{datetime.now().strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S.%f')[:-3]}] [INFO] Starting Lap Timing Diagnostic...", flush=True)
    
    raw_data_queue = Queue()
    
    # We only need these for context in the log, not for DB writes.
    session_handler = SessionHandler()
    stint_handler = StintHandler(session_handler)

    collector = LMUCollector(raw_data_queue=raw_data_queue)
    diagnostic_thread = LapTimingDiagnostic(raw_data_queue, session_handler, stint_handler)
    
    collector.start()
    diagnostic_thread.start()
    
    print(f"[{datetime.now().strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S.%f')[:-3]}] [INFO] Diagnostic running. Waiting for game data...", flush=True)
    print(f"[{datetime.now().strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S.%f')[:-3]}] [INFO] Please perform the test sequence now.", flush=True)
    
    try:
        while True: time.sleep(1)
    except KeyboardInterrupt:
        print(f"\n[{datetime.now().strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S.%f')[:-3]}] [INFO] Shutdown signal received.", flush=True)
    finally:
        collector.stop()
        diagnostic_thread.stop()
        print(f"[{datetime.now().strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S.%f')[:-3]}] [INFO] Diagnostic shut down. Exiting.", flush=True)

if __name__ == '__main__':
    run_daemon()


python daemon.py 2>&1 | Tee-Object -FilePath "lap_timing_diagnostic.txt"

Hypotheses and Assumptions to Verify
Our entire "Progressive Timing" strategy (Approach C) rests on a few key assumptions about the shared memory data. We must prove these are true.
Hypothesis #1 (Sector Transition Signal): The player_scoring.mSector variable changes its value at the precise moment the car crosses a sector boundary line on the track.
Why it's critical: If this signal is delayed or inconsistent, our ability to take accurate timestamps for provisional sector times is compromised.
What we'll look for: A clean change from Sector=1 to Sector=2 at the S1 line, and Sector=2 to Sector=0 at the S2 line.
Hypothesis #2 (Lap Start/End Signal): The combination of mTotalLaps incrementing and mLapDist resetting to near-zero is the definitive, instantaneous signal for a lap crossing, for both flying laps and out-laps.
Why it's critical: This is the anchor point for all our lap-based calculations. It must be 100% reliable.
What we'll look for: Lap changing from X to X+1 at the exact same moment LapDist changes from a large value (e.g., 4273.1) to a small value (e.g., 0.5).
Hypothesis #3 (Timer Consistency): The player_scoring.mLapStartET variable is the "ground truth" for the start time of any given lap, and it updates reliably after a lap is completed. The telemetry.mElapsedTime is the master session clock.
Why it's critical: Our out-lap time calculation (ElapsedTime - LapStartET) depends entirely on these two values being consistent and reliable.
What we'll look for: After a lap crossing, mLapStartET should update to the approximate value of mElapsedTime at the moment of crossing.
Hypothesis #4 (Sector Time Availability): For a flying lap, the mLastSector1 and mLastSector2 values become valid (i.e., > 0) on the frame after the lap is completed, just like mLastLapTime. For an out-lap, they remain invalid (-1 or 0).
Why it's critical: This confirms our hybrid logic. We need to know when we can trust the official sector times versus when we must rely on our own calculated ones.
What we'll look for: The exact frame where LastSec1 and LastSec2 change from -1 to a valid time, relative to the lap crossing.
Test Sequence on Track
To test all these hypotheses, I propose the following simple sequence, which should be performed smoothly.
Start a Practice session.
Click "Drive."
Drive out of the pits and onto the track.
Complete the out-lap, crossing the start/finish line.
Complete one full flying lap.
Stop the car immediately after crossing the S/F line to finish the flying lap. This allows us to get a clean log of the final data transition without it being overwritten by the next lap.
Return to the garage and end the session.
Data Logging Plan
To capture the necessary data with high fidelity, we will again repurpose the diagnostic daemon.py.
Logging Frequency: 50Hz. For this task, higher frequency is better to ensure we don't miss the exact frame of a state change.
Logging Triggers: We need to log around the three most important parts of the track:
200m before and after the Sector 1 line.
200m before and after the Sector 2 line.
200m before and after the Start/Finish line.
Variables to be Logged ([DIAG-FRAME]):
We need a slightly expanded set of variables for this test, focusing heavily on all available timing information.
Identity: Lap (mTotalLaps), Sector (mSector)
Position: LapDist (mLapDist)
Master Clock: ElapsedTime (mElapsedTime)
Lap Timers (Sim):
LapStartET (mLapStartET)
TimeIntoLap (mTimeIntoLap)
Current Sector Timers (Sim):
CurSec1 (mCurSector1)
CurSec2 (mCurSector2)
Last Lap Timers (Sim):
LastLapTime (mLastLapTime)
LastSec1 (mLastSector1)
LastSec2 (mLastSector2)
App State (for context):
AppPlayerState (self.player_state)
AppStintNum (self.stint_handler.current_stint_model.stint_number)
This plan will give us a high-resolution snapshot of every relevant variable changing around the critical boundaries on the track. The resulting log file will provide definitive proof to either validate or reject our hypotheses, allowing us to choose the best lap timing architecture with complete confidence.

This is a perfect log file. It contains everything we need to definitively validate or reject our hypotheses. After a detailed analysis of the data, I can provide clear answers to each of our questions.

The short answer is: **All four of our core hypotheses are validated**, with one critical and very helpful clarification. This is excellent news. It confirms that **Approach C ("Progressive Timing with Official Override") is not only feasible but is the definitively correct architectural choice.**

Here is the detailed, evidence-based breakdown for each hypothesis.

---

### **Hypothesis #1: Sector Transition Signal**

**Status:** **VALIDATED**

The `mSector` variable is a precise, instantaneous signal of a sector boundary crossing. The crucial discovery is that for flying laps, the `mCurSector` timers become valid on the *exact same frame* as the sector change.

*   **Evidence (Sector 1 -> Sector 2 on the flying lap):**
    ```
    // Last frame in Sector 1
    [... 15:42:41.041] [DIAG-FRAME] Lap=1 Sector=1 ... CurSec1=-1.000 CurSec2=-1.000
    
    // --> Boundary Crossing Frame <--
    [... 15:42:41.084] [DIAG-FRAME] Lap=1 Sector=2 ... CurSec1=28.964 CurSec2=-1.000
    ```
    As you can see, on the exact frame that `Sector` flipped to `2`, `CurSec1` was instantly populated with the final, official time for that sector: `28.964`.

*   **Evidence (Sector 2 -> Sector 0 on the flying lap):**
    ```
    // Last frame in Sector 2
    [... 15:43:34.858] [DIAG-FRAME] Lap=1 Sector=2 ... CurSec1=28.964 CurSec2=-1.000

    // --> Boundary Crossing Frame <--
    [... 15:43:34.892] [DIAG-FRAME] Lap=1 Sector=0 ... CurSec1=28.964 CurSec2=82.760
    ```
    The same pattern holds. The moment `Sector` flips to `0` (start of Sector 3), `CurSec2` is populated with its final value of `82.760`.

**Conclusion:** This is perfect. It means we don't need to do any complex application-side timing for the sectors of a *flying lap*. We can simply read the final `mCurSec1` and `mCurSec2` values the moment they become available.

---

### **Hypothesis #2: Lap Start/End Signal**

**Status:** **VALIDATED**

The combination of `mTotalLaps` incrementing and `mLapDist` resetting is an atomic, 100% reliable signal for crossing the start/finish line.

*   **Evidence (Out-lap -> Flying Lap):**
    ```
    // Last frame of Lap 0
    [... 15:42:12.050] [DIAG-FRAME] Lap=0 LapDist=4263.08 ...

    // First frame of Lap 1
    [... 15:42:12.084] [DIAG-FRAME] Lap=1 LapDist=3.19 ...
    ```

*   **Evidence (Flying Lap -> Next Lap):**
    ```
    // Last frame of Lap 1
    [... 15:43:57.445] [DIAG-FRAME] Lap=1 LapDist=4262.73 ...

    // First frame of Lap 2
    [... 15:43:57.479] [DIAG-FRAME] Lap=2 LapDist=2.88 ...
    ```

**Conclusion:** The transition is instantaneous and clean in both cases. This is the solid foundation we need.

---

### **Hypothesis #3: Timer Consistency**

**Status:** **VALIDATED**

The `mElapsedTime` and `mLapStartET` timers are perfectly consistent and behave as expected.

*   **Evidence (Flying Lap Start):**
    ```
    // Last frame of Lap 0
    [... 15:42:12.050] [DIAG-FRAME] ... ElapsedTime=139.192 LapStartET=0.000

    // First frame of Lap 1
    [... 15:42:12.084] [DIAG-FRAME] ... ElapsedTime=139.213 LapStartET=139.118
    ```
    The `mLapStartET` for the new lap (Lap 1) was set to `139.118`, which is the approximate `ElapsedTime` at the moment of crossing.

*   **Evidence (Flying Lap End):**
    *   The `LapStartET` for Lap 1 was `139.118`.
    *   The `ElapsedTime` on the final frame of Lap 1 was `244.572`.
    *   The calculated lap time is `244.572 - 139.118 = 105.454`.
    *   The official `mLastLapTime` that appears on the next frame is `105.405`.
    *   This is a negligible difference of only `0.049` seconds, which is perfectly acceptable and likely due to the exact tick the sim uses internally.

**Conclusion:** The timers are reliable. The formula `ElapsedTime - LapStartET` is a highly accurate way to calculate the total time for any lap, especially the out-lap where no official time is given.

---

### **Hypothesis #4: Sector Time Availability**

**Status:** **VALIDATED with a CRITICAL (and helpful) CORRECTION**

Our original assumption was that the `mLast...` variables would appear one frame *after* the lap counter incremented. The logs show something even better.

*   **Evidence (Flying Lap -> Next Lap):**
    ```
    // Last frame of Lap 1
    [... 15:43:57.445] [DIAG-FRAME] Lap=1 ... LastLapTime=-1.000 LastSec1=-1.000 LastSec2=-1.000

    // --> The Lap Crossing Frame <--
    [... 15:43:57.479] [DIAG-FRAME] Lap=2 ... LastLapTime=105.405 LastSec1=28.964 LastSec2=82.760
    ```

**Conclusion:** The official `mLastLapTime`, `mLastSector1`, and `mLastSector2` values become valid on the **exact same frame** that the `mTotalLaps` counter increments. We do not need to wait an extra frame. This simplifies our logic significantly. Also, as expected, these values remained at `-1.000` after the out-lap, confirming they are only valid for flying laps.

### **Final Verdict and The Path Forward**

This diagnostic run was a massive success. The data has confirmed that **Approach C ("Progressive Timing with Official Override") is the correct architecture.** We have reliable signals for every piece of the puzzle.

Here is the refined logic we can now implement with full confidence:

1.  **For Out-Laps:** We will time the sectors by capturing the `ElapsedTime` at each `mSector` transition. The total lap time will be the sum of these sector times, and also verifiable with `ElapsedTime - LapStartET`.
2.  **For Flying Laps:** We will completely ignore our internally calculated times. On the single frame that `mTotalLaps` increments, we will grab the now-valid `mLastLapTime`, `mLastSector1`, and `mLastSector2` to construct our `LapCompleted` event. This guarantees our data is always identical to the official in-game timing.

We are now ready to write the final, correct code for `lap_detector.py`.
